class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gemini_7_in_orbit_-_GPN-2006-000035.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first <a href="/wiki/Space_rendezvous" title="Space rendezvous">space rendezvous</a> was accomplished by <a href="/wiki/Gemini_6A" title="Gemini 6A">Gemini 6A</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gemini_7" title="Gemini 7">Gemini 7</a> in 1965</div></div></div>\n<p>This is a <b>list of spaceflight records</b>. Most of these records relate to <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human spaceflights</a>, but some unmanned and animal records are listed as well.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" references).\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><br/>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_time_in_space">Most time in space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Most time in space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Russian cosmonaut <a href="/wiki/Gennady_Padalka" title="Gennady Padalka">Gennady Padalka</a>, who has spent 878 days in space over five missions, became the record holder for the most time spent in space when he surpassed, on 28 June 2015, the record of cosmonaut <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Krikalev" title="Sergei Krikalev">Sergei Krikalev</a>, who spent 803 days, 9 hours and 39 minutes (about 2.2 years) in space over the span of six spaceflights on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">Soyuz</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>. <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Malenchenko" title="Yuri Malenchenko">Yuri Malenchenko</a> is currently in second place, having spent 828 days in space on six spaceflights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skk_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-skk-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skk2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-skk2-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p4n_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-p4n-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following is a list of the 50 space travelers with the most total time in space, as of  20&#160;December&#160;2018.<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spacefacts_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spacefacts-17">[17]</a></sup> Travelers currently in space are ranked by total time in space of their completed missions only.\n</p><p>Color key:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:1px solid #AAAAAA; padding:1px .6em; background-color:#99FF99; color:black; TMA-9">Soyuz TMA-9</a>)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopMechDur_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-PopMechDur-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Longest_single_flight_by_a_woman">Longest single flight by a woman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Longest single flight by a woman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>NASA astronaut <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Whitson" title="Peggy Whitson">Peggy Whitson</a> holds the record for the longest single spaceflight by a woman when she surpassed Italian astronaut <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Cristoforetti" title="Samantha Cristoforetti">Samantha Cristoforetti</a>\'s 199 days, 16 hours during <a href="/wiki/Expedition_52" title="Expedition 52">Expedition 52</a> in 2017. She returned to Earth in September 2017, having spent 289 days, 5 hours and 1 minute in space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In third place is American astronaut <a href="/wiki/Sunita_Williams" title="Sunita Williams">Sunita Williams</a> with 195 days<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malik_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malik-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sunita-Bio_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sunita-Bio-30">[30]</a></sup> on the ISS, where she was a member of <a href="/wiki/Expedition_14" title="Expedition 14">Expedition 14</a>/<a href="/wiki/Expedition_15" title="Expedition 15">Expedition 15</a> (2006&#8211;2007).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Longest_continuous_occupation_of_space">Longest continuous occupation of space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Longest continuous occupation of space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>An international partnership consisting of Russia, the United States, Canada, Japan and the member states of the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> have jointly maintained a continuous human presence in space since 31 October 2000, when <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-31" title="Soyuz TM-31">Soyuz TM-31</a> was launched. Two days later it docked with the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MostExtreme_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-MostExtreme-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Year_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-10Year-31">[31]</a></sup> Since then space has been continuously occupied for 18&#160;years, 107&#160;days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MostExtreme_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-MostExtreme-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Longest_continuous_occupation_of_a_spacecraft">Longest continuous occupation of a spacecraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Longest continuous occupation of a spacecraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> has been continuously occupied since 2 November 2000 (18&#160;years, 105&#160;days).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MostExtreme_9-5"><a href="#cite_note-MostExtreme-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Year_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-10Year-31">[31]</a></sup> It broke the record of 9 years and 358 days of the Soviet/Russian Space Station <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a> on 23 October 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Year_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-10Year-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Longest_solo_flight">Longest solo flight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Longest solo flight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Valery_Bykovsky" title="Valery Bykovsky">Valery Bykovsky</a> flew solo for 4 days, 23 hours in <a href="/wiki/Vostok_5" title="Vostok 5">Vostok 5</a> from 14 to 19 June 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The flight set a space endurance record which was broken in 1965 by the (non-solo) <a href="/wiki/Gemini_5" title="Gemini 5">Gemini 5</a> flight. The Apollo program included long solo spaceflight, and during the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_16" title="Apollo 16">Apollo 16</a> mission, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Mattingly" title="Ken Mattingly">T. K. Mattingly</a> orbited solo around the Moon for more than <a href="/wiki/Apollo_16#Mission_insignia" title="Apollo 16">3 days and 9 hours</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Longest_time_on_the_lunar_surface">Longest time on the lunar surface</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Longest time on the lunar surface">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eugene_Cernan" title="Eugene Cernan">Eugene Cernan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Schmitt" title="Harrison Schmitt">Harrison Schmitt</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">Apollo 17</a> mission stayed for 74 hours 59 minutes and 40 seconds (over 3 days) on the lunar surface after they landed on 11 December 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAAP17_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAAP17-33">[33]</a></sup> They performed three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">EVAs</a> (extra-vehicular activity) totaling 22 hours 3 minutes, 57 seconds (as commanders were always the first one out of the LM and the last to get back in, Cernan\'s EVA time was slightly longer).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAAP17_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-NASAAP17-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Longest_time_in_lunar_orbit">Longest time in lunar orbit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Longest time in lunar orbit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ronald_Evans_(astronaut)" title="Ronald Evans (astronaut)">Ronald Evans</a> of <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">Apollo 17</a> mission stayed in lunar orbit for 6 days and 4 hours (148 hours);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> however, for the solo portion of that flight around the Moon, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Mattingly" title="Ken Mattingly">T. K. Mattingly</a> on <a href="/wiki/Apollo_16" title="Apollo 16">Apollo 16</a> spent 1 hour 38 minutes longer than Evans\' solo duration.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Speed_and_altitude_records">Speed and altitude records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Speed and altitude records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Farthest_humans_from_Earth">Farthest humans from Earth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Farthest humans from Earth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">Apollo 13</a> crew (<a href="/wiki/Jim_Lovell" title="Jim Lovell">Jim Lovell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_Haise" title="Fred Haise">Fred Haise</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Swigert" title="Jack Swigert">Jack Swigert</a>), while passing over the far side of the Moon at an altitude of 254&#160;km (158&#160;mi) from the lunar surface, were 400,171&#160;km (248,655&#160;mi) from Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apollo13History_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Apollo13History-35">[35]</a></sup> This record-breaking distance was reached at 0:21 UTC on 15 April 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apollo13History_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Apollo13History-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highest_altitude_for_manned_non-lunar_mission">Highest altitude for manned non-lunar mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Highest altitude for manned non-lunar mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gemini_11" title="Gemini 11">Gemini 11</a> crew <a href="/wiki/Pete_Conrad" title="Pete Conrad">Charles Conrad, Jr.</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_F._Gordon,_Jr." title="Richard F. Gordon, Jr.">Richard F. Gordon, Jr.</a> fired their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agena_Target_Vehicle" title="Agena Target Vehicle">Agena Target Vehicle</a> rocket engine on 14 September 1966, at 40 hours 30 minutes after liftoff and achieved a record apogee altitude of 739.2 nautical miles (1,369.0&#160;km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fastest">Fastest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fastest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_vehicle_speed_records#Spacecraft" title="List of vehicle speed records">List of vehicle speed records &#167;&#160;Spacecraft</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Apollo_10" title="Apollo 10">Apollo 10</a> crew (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Patten_Stafford" title="Thomas Patten Stafford">Thomas Stafford</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Young_(astronaut)" title="John Young (astronaut)">John W. Young</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eugene_Cernan" title="Eugene Cernan">Eugene Cernan</a>) achieved the highest speed relative to Earth ever attained by humans: 39,897&#160;kilometers per hour (11.082&#160;kilometers per second or 24,791&#160;miles per hour, approximately 32 times the <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_sound" title="Speed of sound">speed of sound</a> and 0.0037 percent of the <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MostExtreme_9-6"><a href="#cite_note-MostExtreme-9">[9]</a></sup> The record was set 26 May 1969.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MostExtreme_9-7"><a href="#cite_note-MostExtreme-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Age_records">Age records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Age records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JohnGlenn.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1987" data-file-width="1590" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/JohnGlenn.jpg/110px-JohnGlenn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/JohnGlenn.jpg/165px-JohnGlenn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/JohnGlenn.jpg/220px-JohnGlenn.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JohnGlenn.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>John Glenn, 14 April 1998</div></div></div>\n<h3><span id="Earliest-born_to_reach_space_.28suborbital_flight.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Earliest-born_to_reach_space_(suborbital_flight)">Earliest-born to reach space (suborbital flight)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Earliest-born to reach space (suborbital flight)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Joseph_A._Walker" title="Joseph A. Walker">Joe Walker</a> (born 20 February 1921), on <a href="/wiki/X-15_Flight_90" title="X-15 Flight 90">X-15 Flight 90</a> on 19 July 1963.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Earliest-born_to_reach_space_.28orbital_flight.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Earliest-born_to_reach_space_(orbital_flight)">Earliest-born to reach space (orbital flight)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Earliest-born to reach space (orbital flight)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Man &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Beregovoy" title="Georgy Beregovoy">Georgy Beregovoy</a> (born 15 April 1921), on <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_3" title="Soyuz 3">Soyuz 3</a> on 26 October 1968.</li>\n<li>Woman &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Tereshkova" title="Valentina Tereshkova">Valentina Tereshkova</a> (born 6 March 1937), on <a href="/wiki/Vostok_6" title="Vostok 6">Vostok 6</a> on 16&#8211;19 June 1963.</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Youngest_.28age_during_spaceflight.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Youngest_(age_during_spaceflight)">Youngest (age during spaceflight)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Youngest (age during spaceflight)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Man &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Gherman_Titov" title="Gherman Titov">Gherman Titov</a> (aged 25 years), on <a href="/wiki/Vostok_2" title="Vostok 2">Vostok 2</a> on 6 August 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MostExtreme_9-8"><a href="#cite_note-MostExtreme-9">[9]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Woman &#8211; Valentina Tereshkova (aged 26 years), on <a href="/wiki/Vostok_6" title="Vostok 6">Vostok 6</a> on 16&#8211;19 June 1963.</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Oldest_.28age_during_spaceflight.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Oldest_(age_during_spaceflight)">Oldest (age during spaceflight)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Oldest (age during spaceflight)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Man &#8211; <a href="/wiki/John_Glenn" title="John Glenn">John Glenn</a> (aged 77), on <a href="/wiki/STS-95" title="STS-95">STS-95</a> on 29 October 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MostExtreme_9-9"><a href="#cite_note-MostExtreme-9">[9]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Woman &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Whitson" title="Peggy Whitson">Peggy Whitson</a> (aged 56), on <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_MS-03" title="Soyuz MS-03">Soyuz MS-03</a> on 17 November 2016. She turned 57 on 9 February 2017, while still in space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spacewalk_records">Spacewalk records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Spacewalk records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cumulative_spacewalk_records" title="List of cumulative spacewalk records">List of cumulative spacewalk records</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_spacewalks">Most spacewalks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Most spacewalks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Man &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Solovyev" title="Anatoly Solovyev">Anatoly Solovyev</a>, 16 spacewalks for a total time of 82 hours, 21 minutes (which is also the duration record).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Woman &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Whitson" title="Peggy Whitson">Peggy Whitson</a>, 10 spacewalks for a total time of 60 hours, 21 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evanine_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-evanine-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVA2017_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-EVA2017-41">[41]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_spacewalks_during_a_single_mission">Most spacewalks during a single mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Most spacewalks during a single mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>7: <a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Solovyev" title="Anatoly Solovyev">Anatoly Solovyev</a>, during the 24th Expedition on the Soviet/Russian space station <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a>, in 1997&#8211;98. (Two were internal "spacewalks" inside a depressurized module.)</li>\n<li>6: <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kizim" title="Leonid Kizim">Leonid Kizim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Solovyov_(cosmonaut)" title="Vladimir Solovyov (cosmonaut)">Vladimir Solovyov</a>, the third crew on the Soviet space station <a href="/wiki/Salyut_7" title="Salyut 7">Salyut 7</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_records">Animal records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Animal records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Animals_in_space" title="Animals in space">Animals in space</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_living_organisms_in_space">First living organisms in space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: First living organisms in space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first living organisms of any kind to enter space were <a href="/wiki/Drosophila_melanogaster" title="Drosophila melanogaster">fruit flies</a> launched by the United States in 1947 aboard a <a href="/wiki/V-2_rocket" title="V-2 rocket">V-2 rocket</a> to an altitude of 68 miles (109&#160;km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceanimals_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-spaceanimals-42">[42]</a></sup> They were also the first animals to safely return from space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceanimals_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-spaceanimals-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_animal_in_orbit">First animal in orbit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: First animal in orbit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Laika" title="Laika">Laika</a> was a Soviet female <a href="/wiki/Dog" title="Dog">canine</a> launched on 3 November 1957 on <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_2" title="Sputnik 2">Sputnik 2</a>. The technology to de-orbit had not yet been developed, so there was no expectation for survival. She died several hours into flight. <a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_dogs" title="Soviet space dogs">Belka and Strelka</a> became the first canines to safely return to Earth from orbit on 19 August 1960.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Longest_canine_single_flight">Longest canine single flight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Longest canine single flight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Soviet space dogs <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian language text"><a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_dogs#Veterok_and_Ugolyok" title="Soviet space dogs">Veterok</a></i> (<span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">&#1042;&#1077;&#1090;&#1077;&#1088;&#1086;&#1082;</span>, "Light Wind") and <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian language text">Ugolyok</i> (<span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">&#1059;&#1075;&#1086;&#1083;&#1105;&#1082;</span>, "Ember") were launched on 22 February 1966 on board <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmos_110" title="Cosmos 110">Cosmos 110</a> and spent 22 days in orbit before landing on 16 March.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_animals_beyond_low-Earth_orbit">First animals beyond low-Earth orbit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: First animals beyond low-Earth orbit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>An assortment of animals including a pair of <a href="/wiki/Russian_tortoise" title="Russian tortoise">Russian tortoises</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Piophila" title="Piophila">wine flies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mealworm" title="Mealworm">mealworms</a> launched with a number of other biological specimens including <a href="/wiki/Seed" title="Seed">seeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> on a <a href="/wiki/Circumlunar_trajectory" title="Circumlunar trajectory">circumlunar</a> mission aboard the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Zond_5" title="Zond 5">Zond 5</a> spacecraft on 15 September 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceanimals_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-spaceanimals-42">[42]</a></sup> It was launched by a <a href="/wiki/Proton-K" title="Proton-K">Proton-K</a> rocket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceanimals_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-spaceanimals-42">[42]</a></sup> The capsule came within 2,000 kilometres (1,200&#160;mi) of the Moon and later successfully returned to Earth, the first spacecraft in history to return safely to Earth from the Moon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceanimals_42-4"><a href="#cite_note-spaceanimals-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_unmanned_spaceflights">Notable unmanned spaceflights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight_records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notable unmanned spaceflights">edit</a><span (24,000,000 kilometres (15,000,000 mi)).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Spacecraft will continue to lower its perihelion by multiple Venus gravity assists until its closest approach in 2024, which is expected to bring the probe within 9.86 solar radii (6,900,000 km; 4,300,000 mi) of the Sun\'s surface at a velocity of  191.7 km/s (690,000 km/h; 430,000 mph)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>, by which point it will have become the fastest object in the Solar System apart from Comets (overtaking asteroid <a href="/wiki/2005_HC4" title="2005 HC4">2005 HC4</a>).\n</p>\n</td>\n<td><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img
